_Closure: FR14n Story State `fixes-pending → done`; Status `fixes-pending → done`; sprint-status row `2-4: review → done`; Epic 2 counter 3/17 `done` → 4/17 `done`; PR #230 stays Draft (Epic 2 closes at Story 2.17). Fifth Epic-2 CR re-run ZERO-PATCH closure (Story 2.1 iter-133 / 2.2 iter-154 / 2.3 iter-171 / 2.4 iter-183); 6-iter Story 2.4 chain at forecast (trace + SM + opener + 5-PATCH drain + CR re-run = 6)._

- **RR-D1 — mv onto `COMPOSED_WHITELIST` precedes reload-egress.sh success check, creating disk/kernel drift window on reload failure.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:343-358`. _Nature:_ `cmd_sync` does atomic `mv "${tempfile}" "${COMPOSED_WHITELIST}"` + chmod + trap-clear at lines 343-346, THEN invokes `reload-egress.sh` at :352. If reload returns non-zero, `COMPOSED_WHITELIST` on disk reflects the new staged state while the kernel's active ruleset stays on the previous policy (reload-egress.sh's own fail-closed contract). No fail-open at the kernel layer (reload-egress.sh correctly rolls back on nft/dnsmasq failure); PREVIOUS_COMPOSED intentionally NOT updated on reload-fail path (lines 350-351) so next sync's diff baseline stays correct. However, tools that read COMPOSED_WHITELIST as "current active allow-list ground truth" (none in the 1.0 codebase — reload-egress.sh reads it as INPUT, not as state-of-truth) would disagree with kernel state during the fail-window. _Defer reason:_ cosmetic diagnostic-only under reload failure; no AC violation (AC 3 fail-closed preserved at kernel layer); next sync converges either via operator retry or via automatic healthcheck (Story 2.13 future). Future-Ralph refinement: snapshot+restore `COMPOSED_WHITELIST` on reload-fail OR pass `tempfile` path to reload-egress.sh and rename onto canonical path only on reload success. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.13 (healthcheck on dnsmasq/sshd)** — natural home since healthcheck semantics need to reason about "intended vs applied" policy; OR **post-1.0 CLI polish iteration** if a simpler snapshot+restore approach is preferred.
- **RR-D2 — `$(cat "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}")` round-trip adds trailing newline when source file lacks one.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:412-416`. _Nature:_ `existing="$(cat "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}")"` in `cmd_add` uses command substitution, which strips trailing newlines per POSIX semantics. Then `printf '%s\n' "${existing}"` re-emits the content with a terminating `\n`. Net effect: if operator hand-edited `whitelist.local.txt` without a final newline, the first `cmd_add` normalises it to end in `\n`. This is benign normalisation (POSIX convention dictates text files end in `\n`) but operators who deliberately preserved the no-trailing-newline form may observe an unexpected byte-level mutation. Command substitution also strips NUL bytes silently (only relevant if the file was ever corrupted — impossible via CLI; possible via out-of-band hand-edit). _Defer reason:_ benign normalisation; aligns with POSIX convention; no data corruption. The scale concern (O(size) memory for the round-trip) is vacuous — whitelist.local.txt is expected to be <100 entries. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — refactor to `{ [[ -f "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}" ]] && cat "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}"; printf '%s\n' "${domain}"; } > "${tempfile}"` with optional `tail -c1` probe to preserve original form.
- **RR-D3 — `printf '%s\n' "${additions}"` in diff summary emits a trailing blank line between `+` additions and `-` removals.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:334,339,367`. _Nature:_ `additions` and `removals` are pre-newline-terminated (each is output of `awk 'NF{print ...}' | sort`). `printf '%s\n' "${non-empty}"` adds a stray `\n` between additions block and removals block. Cosmetic: diff summary still readable and parseable, but renders with a blank line separator instead of a tight `+…\n-…` block. No functional defect; SC-7 "grouped +/-" contract preserved at the alphabetical-within-group level. _Defer reason:_ cosmetic formatting only. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 docs/output polish** — switch to `echo "${additions}"` OR `printf '%s' "${additions}$(echo)"` to omit trailing `\n` when followed by more output.
- **RR-D4 — GNU `diff --new-line-format` / `--old-line-format` flags not portable to BSD/macOS diff.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:318`. _Nature:_ `diff --new-line-format='+%L' --old-line-format='-%L' --unchanged-line-format='' prev new || true` uses GNU-diff-specific format-string extensions. Story 2.4 ships the IN-CONTAINER CLI (SC-16 operator invocation locus) where diff is GNU coreutils 9.4 — portable within that scope. The concern: when Story 2.6 lands host-side `pnpm devbox:whitelist` wrapper that `docker exec`s the script, the macOS/BSD host diff is never invoked (exec'd inside the container). So the portability concern is vacuous at 1.0. However, the `|| true` mask would swallow a GNU-diff failure silently, misreporting the SC-7 diff summary. _Defer reason:_ out of Story 2.4 scope — host-side portability is Story 2.6's concern AND the `|| true` mask is a separate defensive-nit (the in-container runtime diff has no failure mode that `|| true` would mask — sources are pre-validated by validate_sources + tempfile is in-memory-then-file). _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 (host-side pnpm devbox:* CLI surface)** — if the wrapper ever composes diff on host, swap to `comm -23`/`comm -13` on pre-sorted inputs (POSIX-portable).
- **RR-D5 — `compose_whitelist_into` silent-skips fragment that becomes unreadable between `find` enumeration and `cat`.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter (defensive-nit). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:200-205`. _Nature:_ TOCTOU race: `validate_sources` enumerates sources (exit 3 on first-seen-unreadable); `compose_whitelist_into` re-enumerates (`[[ -r "${fragment}" ]] || continue` silently skips). If a fragment becomes unreadable between the two enumerations (permissions change, deletion, mount unmount), validate passes and compose silently drops the fragment — resulting allow-list is a SUBSET of expected. Fail-closed safe (smaller allow-list means legitimate traffic is dropped, not extra traffic allowed). _Defer reason:_ very narrow race window (microseconds between two enumerations in the same process); fail-closed outcome; no security exposure. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — symmetric exit-3 on unreadable fragment in `compose_whitelist_into` OR fd-based open-held-across-both-ops.
- **RR-D6 — `cmd_add` persists new domain to disk even when pre-existing sibling lines fail `validate_sources` in the subsequent `cmd_sync`.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:319-327`. _Nature:_ Precondition: operator hand-edited an invalid line into `whitelist.local.txt` (SC-1 positions add/remove as canonical mutation surface — this precondition is non-canonical use). Flow: `cmd_add valid.com` validates the arg (passes), atomic-writes `whitelist.local.txt` (persists `valid.com`), releases mutation lock, invokes `cmd_sync`. cmd_sync runs `validate_sources` → sees the pre-existing invalid line → exits 2. Disk state: `whitelist.local.txt` advanced with the new valid domain. Kernel state: previous policy (no reload invoked; fail-closed). Disk-vs-policy divergence until operator fixes the invalid line + re-syncs. Recovery path: fix invalid line, run `sync`, converges. No security/correctness violation; fail-closed holds. _Defer reason:_ narrow precondition (non-canonical operator hand-edit); self-recovering; fail-closed. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — (a) validate all sources BEFORE `mv` in cmd_add (atomic precondition), OR (b) rollback `whitelist.local.txt` to pre-add state on cmd_sync validate-fail.
- **RR-D7 — `cmd_add` allows substrate-duplicate into `whitelist.local.txt`; `cmd_remove` blocks its cleanup via substrate-protection.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:293-298,456-478`. _Nature:_ `cmd_add github.com` where `github.com` is already in `whitelist/anthropic.txt` fragment: idempotency check at :293-298 only reads `WHITELIST_LOCAL` (not composed union), so the append proceeds — `whitelist.local.txt` now has a redundant `github.com` entry. Later `cmd_remove github.com` hits substrate-protection at :456-478 → exit 2 (per SC-1 "remove cannot edit substrate"). The redundant L-entry is wedged in `whitelist.local.txt` with no CLI-based removal path. Workaround: operator hand-edits `whitelist.local.txt` (it's the operator's own file per SC-2/SC-3, NOT substrate). Fail-closed preserved: `sort -u` dedupes the duplicate in composed output; kernel ruleset is correct. _Defer reason:_ CLI-usability gap, not correctness defect. Operator has a clear workaround (hand-edit own file). _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — on cmd_add, compose substrate (default + fragments) and skip append if domain is already covered. Consistent with SC-4 "additive-only composition" — redundant L-entry adds no policy, should be a no-op.
- **RR-D8 — `mktemp` / `mkdir -p /run` / `mktemp "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}.XXXXXX.tmp"` produce uninformative errors under read-only DEVBOX_DIR or read-only rootfs.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:286-288,302,489`. _Nature:_ Under adverse environments (CI sandbox with ro-mount, hardened container with /run on ro overlay, security-hardened devbox derivative), `mktemp` or `mkdir -p` fails with raw coreutils stderr ("mktemp: failed to create file via template", "mkdir: cannot create directory") — no `whitelist:` log prefix, no SC-11 exit-3 wrapping, no operator-targeted context. `set -e` propagates the non-zero rc correctly (fail-loud), but diagnosability is poor. _Defer reason:_ adverse-environment diagnostic-only; 1.0 devbox runtime has /run as writable tmpfs + DEVBOX_DIR writable (verified Story 2.1 iter-127 bake). _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.5 container-hardening sweep** — when tmpfs/named-volume topology is revised, add writability probes at ensure_run_dir + cmd_add/cmd_remove entry; log contextual `exit 3` with diagnostic.
- **RR-D9 — `cmd_remove` leaves zero-byte `whitelist.local.txt` after removing the last entry instead of unlinking.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:497-504`. _Nature:_ When `whitelist.local.txt` contains one entry and operator removes it, `grep -Fxv` yields empty tempfile; `mv` replaces target with zero-byte file. `stat` / `ls -la` shows file present; `cmd_list` shows zero L-entries; compose pipeline correctly reads empty file as zero additions (fail-closed preserved). Asymmetric with SC-9's "remove with non-existent target = no-op success" semantics: a file that was deleted vs never-existed is not distinguished in CLI UX. _Defer reason:_ cosmetic; no policy impact. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — `[[ -s "${tempfile}" ]] || rm -f "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}"` after mv, mirroring SC-9 symmetry.
- **RR-D10 — `cmd_list` reads sources without shared lock.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:519-563`. _Nature:_ `cmd_list` reads `whitelist.default.txt` + `whitelist/*.txt` fragments + `whitelist.local.txt` without acquiring fd-201 mutation lock. Concurrent `cmd_add`/`cmd_remove` atomic-mv can produce split-brain source attribution: the same domain might be labelled `L` in one scan (read after remove's mv of empty file) and `F:<frag>` in a later invocation. `mv` on same-fs is kernel-atomic, so partial-file reads are impossible — but `list`'s multi-file scan is NOT atomic across files, so the snapshot is inconsistent under high-concurrency. No state corruption (list is read-only); attribution cosmetic drift only. _Defer reason:_ diagnostic-only; list is read-only. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — `flock -s -w 10 201 || exit 4` shared lock over the full scan; pairs with cmd_list's existing fd-201 convention in cmd_add/cmd_remove.
- **RR-D11 — `cp -f "${COMPOSED_WHITELIST}" "${PREVIOUS_COMPOSED}"` is non-atomic; SIGKILL/crash between reload success and snapshot update leaves PREVIOUS_COMPOSED stale.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:357-358`. _Nature:_ Sequence: reload-egress.sh returns 0 at :352, then `cp -f COMPOSED → PREVIOUS` at :357-358. Window between these two steps: SIGKILL/poweroff leaves PREVIOUS_COMPOSED reflecting the PRE-reload state while kernel state reflects POST-reload. Next sync's SC-7 diff misreports additions/removals (shows all reloaded domains as "new" relative to stale previous). No policy impact (kernel is correctly on current policy); cosmetic diff-on-next-sync misattribution. Converges on next successful sync (PREVIOUS gets updated). _Defer reason:_ narrow crash window; self-correcting. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** — `cp -f` to adjacent tempfile then `mv` for atomic snapshot update; OR `ln -f COMPOSED PREVIOUS` (hardlink) if same-fs, avoiding the copy entirely.
- **RR-D12 — Locale-sensitive DOMAIN_REGEX via bash `[[ =~ ]]` under non-C `LC_CTYPE`.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter (new angle; pairs with iter-177 opener D1 defer). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:155`. _Nature:_ bash `[[ =~ ]]` honours `LC_CTYPE` in some implementations. Under locales where `[0-9]` in POSIX bracket expressions expands to Unicode digits (Arabic-Indic, Devanagari), the validator could accept digits that dnsmasq/nft reject downstream. In-container runtime is `C.UTF-8` (Ubuntu 24.04 default) where `[0-9]` is ASCII-only — zero active exposure. When Story 2.6 lands host-side pnpm wrappers, macOS operators may have `LC_CTYPE=en_US.UTF-8` where behavior is implementation-defined. _Defer reason:_ vacuous in current runtime; downstream fail-closed. Subsumes iter-177 opener defer D1 (which also called out `LC_ALL=C` scoping) — narrower in scope but same remediation. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 host-side pnpm CLI wrapping** — add `LC_ALL=C` local scoping at validate_domain + validate_sources sites; mirrors `LC_ALL=C` used on `sort -u` at :214.
- **RR-D13 — `mv tempfile whitelist.local.txt` clobbers symlink target if operator symlinked `whitelist.local.txt` for shared fork state.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:319,503`. _Nature:_ An operator who symlinks `whitelist.local.txt → /shared/whitelist.txt` (e.g., multi-devbox fork with shared overrides) would see: `mv tempfile whitelist.local.txt` removes the symlink and replaces with a regular file on first mutation, breaking the shared-state contract. Subsequent devboxes see stale state. Undocumented usage — the 1.0 spec does not mention symlinks; SC-2 positions the override as a gitignored per-fork file (not cross-fork shared). _Defer reason:_ unusual fork setup; undocumented usage; operator self-assumed the symlink semantic. _Carry-to:_ **post-1.0 CLI polish** OR **docs clarification** — at cmd_add/cmd_remove entry, reject symlinked override (`[[ ! -L "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}" ]]`) with operator-education message pointing to `docker volume` / bind-mount patterns for cross-devbox sharing.

## Deferred from: code review of story-2-5 (2026-04-22)

_Iter-190 `/bmad-code-review (args: "2")` CR opener against cumulative Story 2.5 substrate diff (`b2533b0..HEAD` / 8 SC-19 in-scope files / 413 lines) produced 6 PATCH + **4 DEFER** + ~17 DISMISS. The four deferred items are all integration-boundary or scope-extension concerns sanctioned by spec (SC-14, SC-10) or deferrable to downstream stories. None block the iter-196 `fixes-pending → sm-verified → done` CR-closure gate; all are carried over to Story 2.6 (host-side CLI + operator-migration docs), Story 2.17 (runtime compose-shape check), or operator-workstation smoke._

- **AR-7 — /run writes under USER dev fail for whitelist.sh state files + dnsmasq pid-file.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-190 (probes EC3 + EC12 + EC13 merged). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:198,286,341` + `packages/devbox/scripts/start-egress.sh:30-32` + `packages/devbox/dnsmasq/dnsmasq.conf:52`. _Nature:_ Under USER dev (Dockerfile:268), processes run as UID 1000. `/run` in the Ubuntu base image is root:root mode 0755; dev cannot mkdir/write. Whitelist.sh expects to mktemp/flock/write under `/run/keel-whitelist-*` (lines 198/286/341); start-egress.sh expects `/run/keel-whitelist.composed.txt` + `/run/dnsmasq.pid` + `/run/keel-egress-tailer.pid`; dnsmasq expects `/run/dnsmasq.pid`. All fail EACCES if Docker's tmpfs auto-mount at /run does NOT preserve image-layer ownership. _Defer reason:_ SC-14 branch (ii) is the explicit Story 2.5 spec for this — if operator-workstation smoke surfaces ownership problem, relocation to `/tmp/keel-state/` is a Story 2.6 carry-over. iter-187 assumed SC-14 branch (i) happy path (Docker tmpfs auto-mount preserves image-layer ownership established by `RUN chown dev:dev /run` at Dockerfile-build time, which Story 2.5 did NOT add — branch (i) relies on implicit tmpfs-auto-mount-preserves-image-ownership which is uncertain). _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 host-side `pnpm devbox:*` CLI surface** — which is the scope-owner of `scripts/whitelist.sh` entry-points + is-in-scope to relocate state files. Concrete remediation: either (a) Dockerfile pre-creates `/run` as dev-owned (`RUN chown dev:dev /run` — may not survive Docker's tmpfs auto-mount) OR (b) relocate all `/run/keel-*` paths to `/tmp/keel-state/` (tmpfs with `exec=false,suid=false` is fine for state files) across whitelist.sh + start-egress.sh + reload-egress.sh + dnsmasq.conf. Branch (b) is scope-extensive but avoids the tmpfs-ownership-empirics uncertainty.

- **AR-8 — Fork `docker-compose.override.yml` may replace `volumes:` stanza or strip `NET_BIND_SERVICE` from `cap_add`.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-190 (probes EC10 + EC15 merged). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml:118-125,154-155`. _Nature:_ Compose's default merge strategy for `services.<svc>.volumes` + `services.<svc>.cap_add` arrays is REPLACE (not merge) — a fork's `docker-compose.override.yml` with a differently-shaped `volumes:` block or `cap_add:` list silently bypasses the `INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume` invariant. Upstream cc-devbox pattern `./dev-home:/home/dev:delegated` bind-mount is an obvious override-replacement that would leak Claude Code OAuth tokens to host filesystem, defeating NFR10. NET_BIND_SERVICE strip (e.g., a fork using the drafted AC 2 two-cap list) produces dnsmasq :53-bind EPERM at runtime. _Defer reason:_ SC-10 explicitly defers the active runtime compose-shape check to Story 2.17 / `packages/keel-invariants/src/check-devbox-compose-shape.ts`. Story 2.5 ships the invariant surface + Story 1.9 sync-gate provides static-drift detection of the sourcePath doc; compose-override runtime parse-and-assert is a distinct concern with its own test matrix. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.17 `check-devbox-compose-shape.ts` check** — parses `docker-compose.yml` + any `docker-compose.override.yml` at pre-merge time; asserts `volumes.keel_home_dev` stanza + `cap_add` list membership (NET_ADMIN + NET_RAW + NET_BIND_SERVICE); rejects accidental bind-mount drift or cap-strip. Pairs with the `INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume` invariant ID already registered at 1.0.

- **AR-9 — `/etc/resolv.conf` + `/etc/dnsmasq.conf` writes from reload-egress.sh + start-egress.sh fail EACCES under USER dev.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-190 (probe EC9). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/start-egress.sh:50,60` + `packages/devbox/scripts/reload-egress.sh:119,158,288-289`. _Nature:_ start-egress.sh pins `/etc/resolv.conf` to `nameserver 127.0.0.1` at boot (SC-13 of Story 2.3). Under USER dev, /etc/resolv.conf (Docker bind-mount managed; typically root-owned) and /etc/dnsmasq.conf (root-owned) are unwriteable by UID 1000. start-egress.sh:56 `log "FATAL: cannot write /etc/resolv.conf — ${resolv_err}"` branch will fire; container fail-closes at boot. Egress initialisation never completes. _Defer reason:_ Fix is scope-extensive — options are (a) chown /etc/resolv.conf + /etc/dnsmasq.conf at image-build time (risky: /etc/resolv.conf is Docker-managed at runtime; bind-mount typically preserves host perms), (b) scope-extend to edit Story 2.3 primitive scripts to run under sudo-effective or as a setuid helper (SC-19 forbidden — scripts/start-egress.sh + scripts/reload-egress.sh are explicitly Story-2.3-owned), (c) compose-level `user: root` override for the specific RUN (conflicts with USER dev intent), (d) pre-seed /etc/dnsmasq.conf + /etc/resolv.conf with dev ownership AND accept Docker's bind-mount override of resolv.conf. None is clean at Story 2.5's SC-19 boundary. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 host-side CLI + scope-extension** — the fix belongs with the first story that legitimately touches Story 2.3 scripts for a non-scope-creep reason. Alternatively, operator-workstation smoke may surface a surprise (e.g. Docker's bind-mount of /etc/resolv.conf preserves the image-layer ownership such that dev CAN write to it) which would retire this defer in-place. iter-187 did NOT exercise runtime egress initialisation — the FIRST operator-workstation boot is the adjudicating event.

- **AR-10 — Pre-Story-2.5 named-volume re-use preserves root-owned `/home/dev` tree.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-190 (probe EC2). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml:74-76,154-155` (volume lifecycle). _Nature:_ If an operator has a `keel_home_dev` (or project-prefixed `devbox_keel_home_dev` / `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` depending on AI-3 resolution) volume from a pre-Story-2.5 container run (when processes ran as root and /home/dev files were root-owned), Docker sees the volume non-empty on Story 2.5 container start and SKIPS populate-from-image semantics — the root-owned tree mounts over /home/dev. Under USER dev + dropped CAP_CHOWN, entrypoint's chown calls fail silently per SC-5 expected-failure posture. Claude Code OAuth (Story 2.8) + gh login (Story 2.9) + shell history + vim swap files all EACCES on write. No diagnostic is emitted; operator must manually `docker volume rm <name>` to recover. _Defer reason:_ Fresh-volume first-boot happy path per SC-6 is not regressed; only pre-existing-volume migrations surface the issue. No current-state regression; requires operator education OR detection logic. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 operator-migration documentation** — add a § Upgrading from pre-Story-2.5 images sub-section to `packages/devbox/README.md § Hardening` documenting the `docker volume rm` recovery procedure + the first-boot `stat /home/dev` diagnostic. Alternatively, add a boot-time entrypoint detection (`stat -c '%u' /home/dev` ≠ 1000 → emit WARN) — that path touches entrypoint.sh which is in Story 2.5's SC-19 allow list, but empirical detection-under-dropped-CAP_CHOWN is itself fragile; docs-first is the cleaner 1.0 posture.

## Deferred from: code review of story-2-5 closure (2026-04-22)

_Iter-197 `/bmad-code-review (args: "2")` CR-closure re-run against same `b2533b0..HEAD` diff baseline (9 SC-19 in-scope files post-drain, 645 lines) produced **ZERO-PATCH close** + **2 DEFER** + ~13 DISMISS. Acceptance Auditor verdict: all 5 ACs + 19 SCs satisfied; CR drain complete; all 6 AI-1..AI-6 opener patches verified landed without regression. The two new DEFERs below are operator-docs / Story-2.6-scope concerns surfaced only on re-read of the post-drain state (not visible at opener due to being downstream-of-drain observations). Neither blocks `fixes-pending → sm-verified → done` closure._

- **AR-11 — `KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_{TMP,VARTMP}_MB` envvar validation missing.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-197 (probe EC3). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml:~153-155` (tmpfs long-syntax with `size=${KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_TMP_MB:-2048}m`). _Nature:_ Operator setting `KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_TMP_MB=0` (or empty / negative / non-numeric like `"2gb"`) passes Compose variable-substitution verbatim to the kernel tmpfs mount. `size=0m` produces a zero-byte tmpfs (every write ENOSPC — affects reload-egress.sh mktemp, entrypoint.sh chown_err mktemp, dnsmasq temp-alloc). Non-numeric values produce Compose parse errors at `compose up` time. Fail-closed intact (operator sees unambiguous startup failure), but better DX warrants entrypoint-level preflight (is-numeric + positive-bounds) OR host-side pnpm-CLI preflight. _Defer reason:_ SC-18 pins Story 2.2 as the owner of `KEEL_DEVBOX_*` knob definitions; Story 2.5 consumes the knobs but does NOT own validation. Better-fit surface is Story 2.6 (`pnpm devbox:*` host-side CLI) where envvar preflight is natural. Neither AC 3 nor SC-8 demands runtime validation — both ACs are satisfied by the tmpfs stanza being *parameterized correctly*; validating operator input is hygiene, not contract. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 `pnpm devbox:*` host-side CLI surface** (primary) — add preflight validator that reads `.envrc` (or operator env), confirms `KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_TMP_MB` + `KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_VARTMP_MB` are positive-integer strings matching `^[1-9][0-9]*$` with a soft upper bound (e.g. ≤ 16384 = 16 GB). Alternative: **Story 2.2 amendment PR** — add a bash assertion in `packages/devbox/.envrc.example` (via a `_validate_keel_devbox_envvars` function sourced at enter-directory time).

- **AR-12 — `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` / `-p` CLI flag overrides `name: keel-devbox` top-level key; verification-command volume FQN prefix drifts.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-197 (probe EC6). _Location:_ `packages/devbox/README.md § Hardening § Verification` (`docker volume inspect keel-devbox_keel_home_dev`) + `docs/invariants/devbox-hardening.md § Verification` (same command). _Nature:_ Compose v2 documented precedence for project name resolution: `-p` CLI flag > `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` env > top-level `name:` in compose file > directory basename. The `name: keel-devbox` top-level key added at AI-3 drain (iter-194) pins the substrate default, but a fork operator setting `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME=myfork` resolves the volume FQN as `myfork_keel_home_dev` instead of `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev`. The documented `docker volume inspect keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` command fails with "No such volume"; AC 4 verification under fork override requires substituting the fork's project name in the FQN. _Defer reason:_ Standard documented Compose behavior — not a substrate regression. AC 4 still SATISFIED (named-volume contract held; only the volume's FQN prefix changes per Compose precedence). Verification-command prose could qualify ("where `keel-devbox` is your Compose project name; substitute `${COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_keel_home_dev` for forks with custom project names"). Cosmetic, not load-bearing. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.6 operator-migration docs** — qualify the verification commands in both README and invariant-doc with a one-line note about Compose project-name override precedence. Alternatively, rewrite verification to use `docker compose -p keel-devbox ... config --format json | jq .volumes` so the project name is explicit in the invocation. Neither changes substrate behavior; pure docs polish.

## Deferred from: code review of story-2-6 (2026-04-22)

_Iter-204 `/bmad-code-review (args: "2")` opener against cumulative Story 2.6 substrate diff (`65ef3a3..HEAD` / 26 files / 2152 insertions). Three-layer adversarial fan-out: Blind Hunter + Edge Case Hunter + Acceptance Auditor. Acceptance Auditor: ZERO PATCH-or-higher AC deviations (all 9 ACs + 25 SCs satisfied; SC-15 monitor-pin + SC-9 bare-`running` + 2× invariant contentHash refresh verified legitimate). Code-quality triage: 11 PATCH (AI-1..AI-11; mirrored to story file `## Review Findings § Code Review (iter-204, v1.2) — fixes-pending`) + **7 DEFERs (AR-13..AR-19 below)** + 6 DISMISSED. None of the 7 DEFERs blocks `fixes-pending → sm-verified → done`; all are scope-boundary, intentional-design, or carry-forward items._

- **AR-13 — `start.sh` accepts bare `running` as healthy on first poll → 30 s grace + 120 s timeout are dead code in pre-Story-2.13 substrate.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/start.sh:73-77`. _Nature:_ The poll loop's `case "${health}" in healthy|running)` arm exits 0 immediately. Until Story 2.13 wires a real `HEALTHCHECK` directive into `docker-compose.yml`, `docker inspect ... .State.Health.Status` is empty so the template fallback at line 71 returns `.State.Status = running` immediately after `docker compose up -d` returns. The 30 s grace deadline (line 62) and 120 s healthcheck timeout (line 30) are effectively unreachable. The header docstring (lines 14-21) advertises healthcheck-poll behaviour the implementation does not deliver in the current substrate. _Defer reason:_ SC-9 explicitly designates this as the stub-friendly pre-Story-2.13 posture: "accept `healthy`, `starting` (within first 30s grace), or bare `running` (when no healthcheck is configured — pre-Story-2.13 posture)". Acceptance Auditor verified intentional. Story 2.13 is the healthcheck-definition scope-owner; activating the dead branches is its responsibility. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.13** — when `HEALTHCHECK` is wired into docker-compose.yml + Dockerfile, the `running` arm should be removed (or scoped to "no-healthcheck-configured" detection only) and the grace + timeout become live. Add a Story 2.13 verification step that exercises start.sh against a healthcheck that takes 35-45 s to flip to `healthy` (validates the grace + timeout windows are reached).

- **AR-14 — `env-check.sh` treats explicit empty-string (`KEEL_DEVBOX_DNS_UPSTREAM=`) as "present" rather than "missing".** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/env-check.sh:67-68,95`. _Nature:_ The presence check at line 95 (`[[ -z "${parsed[${v}]+x}" ]]`) tests for KEY existence in the associative array, not value emptiness. An operator who writes `KEEL_DEVBOX_DNS_UPSTREAM=` (explicit empty) passes the missing-var check. Downstream consumers (compose variable substitution, dnsmasq.conf) may fail later with no env-check hint. The shape-validator at line 100-109 covers tmpfs MB knobs but NOT integer/path-typed knobs like `KEEL_DEVBOX_PORT_*`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_CPUS`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_NOFILE`. _Defer reason:_ The comment block at lines 67-68 explicitly documents the intentional posture: "operators may explicitly set `X=` to signal 'present but empty'". SC-14 scope was integer-shape validation (tmpfs MB) only; non-integer empty-string treatment remains an explicit design decision. AC 8 satisfied by the presence-of-name check. _Carry-to:_ **Future ergonomic-pass story** — extend the shape validator to cover all positive-integer knobs (`KEEL_DEVBOX_PORT_*`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_CPUS`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_NOFILE`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_MEMORY_GB`, `KEEL_DEVBOX_SHM_GB`) AND optionally a `SHAPE_NONEMPTY` set for stringly-typed required knobs. Alternative: Story 2.7+ may refactor the validator into a shared `_validate.sh` library if the host-side CLI grows further envvar-checking surface.

- **AR-15 — `start.sh` TOCTOU between `docker image inspect` and `docker compose up -d`.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/start.sh:39-58`. _Nature:_ Line 39 inspects `${IMAGE_TAG}` (default `keel-devbox:local`) for fast-fail exit-10 when the image is missing. Between line 42 (inspect-pass) and line 58 (`docker compose up -d devbox`), an external `docker rmi` could remove the image, OR the image could be present but corrupt (truncated download), OR compose could pull/build a different SHA than was inspected. start.sh has no SHA pinning — there's no detection of "image present but stale". _Defer reason:_ Compose handles the actual build/pull and emits its own error if the image is unavailable at `up` time; the inspect check is a fast-fail UX hint, not a correctness gate. The script header (line 19) documents "image not built (run `pnpm devbox:build` first)" as a best-effort hint. AC 3 satisfied — start succeeds when the image is present and compose-up returns clean. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.13 healthcheck integration OR a future image-provenance hardening story** — pin the expected image SHA in `INV-devbox-image-provenance` (new invariant) + assert it at start.sh, similar to the contentHash pattern used by `INV-prek-prepare-lifecycle`. Out of Story 2.6 scope.

- **AR-16 — `shell.sh` argument forwarding pattern `bash -l "$@"` rejects bare commands; `pnpm devbox:shell whoami` errors "No such file or directory".** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/shell.sh:32-34`. _Nature:_ The `bash -l "$@"` pattern interprets the first non-option argument as a SCRIPT FILE, not a command. `pnpm devbox:shell -c 'whoami'` works (bash `-l -c <cmd>` is valid); `pnpm devbox:shell whoami` fails (bash `-l whoami` looks for an executable script named `whoami`). _Defer reason:_ AC 5 specifies "interactive shell as the dev user"; argument forwarding was not in the AC. The script header docstring shows only the no-args interactive form. Operator UX enhancement, not a defect. _Carry-to:_ **Future ergonomic-pass story** — either add a `--help` form documenting the `-c '<cmd>'` constraint, OR detect bare-command invocation and auto-wrap as `bash -l -c "$*"`. Out of Story 2.6 scope.

- **AR-17 — `env-check.sh` quote-stripping is asymmetric: peels one quote each side without checking they match.** _Source:_ Blind Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/env-check.sh:82-83`. _Nature:_ Lines 82-83 (`value="${value#\"}"; value="${value%\"}"`) strip at most one leading and one trailing double quote (and similarly for single quotes) without verifying the quotes paired. A malformed `KEEL_DEVBOX_FOO="5` (unmatched opening quote) becomes `5` silently. _Defer reason:_ Defensive parsing already filters realistic mis-typings via the upstream missing-var check + tmpfs shape regex. Hardening would require quote-state tracking; not load-bearing at 1.0. _Carry-to:_ **Future ergonomic-pass story** OR fold into AR-14 if a broader env-check refactor lands.

- **AR-18 — 12 of 13 scripts lack `--help`/`-h` handling (only `clean.sh:62` has `usage`).** _Source:_ Blind Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/{attach,build,rebuild,start,stop,restart,shell,status,logs,monitor-host,whitelist-host,env-check}.sh`. _Nature:_ Operator running `pnpm devbox:start --help` gets `docker compose up -d --help` output (compose's help, NOT script-level usage). README + AGENTS.md document the verb table externally; per-script `--help` would be more discoverable. _Defer reason:_ AC 1-9 do not mandate per-script `--help`; ergonomic enhancement. _Carry-to:_ **Future ergonomic-pass story** — add a uniform `case "$1" in -h|--help) usage; exit 0 ;; esac` block to each script. Could pair naturally with AR-19 (shared `_lib.sh`).

- **AR-19 — Eight scripts duplicate the `docker info` + `docker inspect .State.Status` pre-flight; sourcing a shared `_lib.sh` would deduplicate ~24 lines and ensure consistent exit-8/exit-9 messaging.** _Source:_ Edge Case Hunter iter-204. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/{start,stop,restart,shell,attach,status,logs,monitor-host,whitelist-host}.sh`. _Nature:_ DRY violation. Any future change to the docker-unreachable hint (e.g., "is colima running?") must touch 8+ files. _Defer reason:_ Refactor opportunity, not bug. Carry to a future cleanup story OR Story 2.7+ when the script set grows further. _Carry-to:_ **Story 2.7+ host-side CLI consolidation** OR **Future hygiene-pass story** — extract `packages/devbox/scripts/_lib.sh` with `_check_docker_info()` + `_check_container_running()` + `_log_with_prefix()` helpers; source from each script's preamble.

## Deferred from: Story 2.6 AI-8 iter-212 (2026-04-22)

_AI-8 drain applied `unset COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` to the 9 CR-flagged container-discovery scripts (start / stop / restart / shell / attach / status / logs / monitor-host / whitelist-host). The sibling drift-vector review surfaces three adjacent scripts outside the CR-flagged set whose `docker compose` invocations are ALSO affected by an operator-shell `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` override. None were flagged by the CR Blind / Edge Case / Acceptance Auditor layers at iter-204; recording here so a future ergonomic-pass or Story 2.7+ host-side consolidation can extend the `unset` uniformly without re-drafting the audit._

- **AR-20 — `clean.sh:113,140` `docker compose down` under `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` override operates on the wrong project label; named-volume destruction with `--with-volumes --force-backend-b` would target `${COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_keel_home_dev` rather than the INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume-pinned `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev`. PROMOTED TO AI-12 iter-217 (re-triaged at iter-216 CR closure; Edge Case Hunter re-scored as PATCH because `--remove-orphans` on the override project reaches unrelated containers — collateral-damage risk higher than the iter-212 "silent no-op" analysis credited).** _Source:_ AI-8 sibling-vector review (iter-212) → promoted at iter-216 CR closure. _Location:_ `packages/devbox/scripts/clean.sh:113,140`. _Nature:_ Same drift class as AI-8 but on the destructive (down-volume) surface rather than container-discovery. An operator with `export COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME=my-fork` plus `pnpm devbox:clean --with-volumes --force-backend-b --yes` would: (a) attempt to remove `my-fork_keel_home_dev` volume (doesn't exist under fresh substrate → no-op) AND (b) LEAVE the real `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` volume untouched (operator intent was "destroy the devbox volume"; actual effect is "destroy nothing") AND (c) `--remove-orphans` removes any `my-fork`-labelled container as collateral damage. Iter-216 closure re-triage weighted (c) above the iter-212 analysis's no-op framing. _Defer reason (SUPERSEDED iter-216):_ Promoted to AI-12 — tracked in story file § Review Findings § Code Review Closure (iter-216). _Carry-to:_ CLOSED — AI-12 LANDED iter-217 (`packages/devbox/scripts/clean.sh:36` `unset COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` with 10-line rationale comment anchoring AR-20 + `INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume`; env-shim smoke confirms CPN unset before first docker call; source-level ordering guard: unset@L36 < first-docker@L125; see story file Change Log v1.14).

The drift is cosmetic: compose-build logs emit `Building service devbox` under the override's project name (`my-fork` instead of `keel-devbox`), and buildkit intermediate image labels carry the wrong project. Operator running `docker image inspect keel-devbox:local` still finds the image; downstream `start.sh` (now AI-8-fixed) finds it too. _Defer reason:_ Cosmetic log drift; no correctness or invariant impact.
